<Author>CaliforniaOntheGoMom
<Content>Great location, cheap parking within walking distance After reading a few reviews on this hotel, I booked it and hoped for the best. The front staff was very friendly and permitted us to check in early on Christmas Day. My sister who was traveling with us was also checked in early.The rooms were nice, not fancy but not subpar, they even had a pillow menu which we never used since we were fine with the pillows we had. The bathroom was tiny but served it's purpose and I would say that would be my only disappointment in the room.We did the buffet the 1st morning but it was alittle pricey. I recommend walking across the street to Cafe Peregonia I believe is the name, its a small place, big portions and nice service. I remember the green awning and that its next to a bicycle shop.Now for parking which is very expensive, DO NOT PARK at the hotel unless you want to part with $40 a day. We parked our cars overnight on the street, BUT we moved it at 7am to nearby parking garages such as the Anchorage Garage for an early bird special of $12 a day, don't bother moving your car from the garage until 7p when the meters do not need to be fed any coins. The cable cars, Ghiradelli square, Fishermans Wharf are all within 3 blks from the hotel and just head up Columbus for great Italian and if you venture further up you will come uopn Chinatown.

<Author>kiwimeggles
<Content>Great hotel in great location Stayed at the holiday inn fishermans wharf in early December. I was travelling alone before meeting up with friends in Las Vegas. This hotel was recommended by my travel agent and i found it to be fantastic. My room was huge with 2 queen beds and a large bathroom and very clean. The staff were very helpful - after arriving from australia and realising i had left tickets at home for various tours the concierge was very helpful in contacting the tour companies for me. This hotel is so close to fishermans wharf, the cannery, Ghiradelli factory and pier 39 . A short 5 mins walk will take you to the powell and hyde cable car. There are plenty of restaurants close by and also a safeway supermarket and walgreens just around the corner. I had no problems walking around the area alone at night, i felt completely safe, there were always plenty of people around. There are two great cafes across the road that offer great and cheap breakfasts if you want to eat out. I would definately stay here again!!!

<Author>gef-atl
<Content>Couldn't have been more perfect Holiday Inns across the US are pretty predictible - uninspiring decor, cookie cutter bathroom, mildly threadbare carpet and occasional elevator issues This Holiday Inn was no exception but has many many plusses - walking distance to Fisherman's Wharf, Ghirardelli Square, Chinatown, Nob Hill, amazingly conscientious staff (ask for Valerie the concierge), attentive housekeeping staff and helpful telephone staff.Now this above average rating comes with a few caveats.Caveat #1: Confirm your reservation. We booked through Priceline as a king, non-smoking room. When we got to the hotel they were going to put us in a double, smoking room. Fortunately they weren't fully booked and could come up with a non-smoking double. Caveat #2: Dining at the hotel (i.e. Denny's) is ridiculously overpriced. Walk three blocks to Buena Vista for a truly remarkable breakfast - or take a leisurely walk to a Farmer's Market (Ferry Building on Wed/Sat or City Hall on Sunday) and stock up your room. Also, Walgreen's across the street is convenient, even if they don't rotate their banana stock very regularly. Caveat #3: Parking at the hotel is also ridiculously expensive ($39/night). A tip for anyone staying here (or near). Go to the Enterprise on Beach Street and do one-day rentals. They have 24-hour return (hard to find in SF) at reserved parking spots for only $10/night for those renting from them. It's WELL worth the couple block walk for cheap parking.Like I mentioned, this is a perfect location for a SF stay if you're planning to enjoy the city and aren't terribly concerned with being pampered. It's a Holiday Inn. You know what you're signing up for!

<Author>MsBrightside79
<Content>Priceline Deal We got this hotel on a Priceline deal for $ 145.00 / night. Stayed there for 3 nights during Fleet Week. Checked-in at the main building but were told our room was in the Annex. No big deal, just a block from the main building. It was a room with 2 comfortable queen beds, spacious, nice bathroom and most importantly .. it was clean. We were on the 4th floor where you could also use a computer for airline check-in - very convenient. Didn't eat at Denny's as other travellers on here described it as overpriced. Just one block down from the Annex you find enough other places to eat at ( e.g. IHOP ). Across the street is a Walgreens, an F-line stop ( Muni - runs from Fisherman's Wharf all the way to the Castro along Market St. ) and the cable car turn-around is only 2 or 3 blocks away. Glad I got it on a Priceline deal as paying the $200-something / night is way overpriced - but you got the location which is worth a lot. Would stay there again but not for the regular offered price on their website.

<Author>510039
<Content>Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf - Perfect. We traveled to San Francisco for a weekend while visiting family in Northern California. We were there for 2 nights and I would say the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf was the perfect hotel for us.The trip wasn't all sunshine and roses, and i will get into that later, but the SF portion of the trip was great.The Hotel. We arrived around 7:30 Friday night. We were put up in the main building, on the 3rd floor. We had 2 double beds, so when I asked if they had any King's left they said yes, but they were in the other building. Rooms were plenty big. Clean. We didn't have a view at all, but thats OK. We were with our 16 month old, so we needed a crib. Called housekeeping when we got to the room, and the crib was there minutes. We tipped housekeeping $2.50 Saturday morning. I know thats not much, but they seemed to really appreciate it. Left us a note thanking us, and then every time they saw one of us they asked where the baby was (sleeping) and always said hi. The Location. Absolutely perfect. Just a block from the Cannery  Ghirardelli Square. 2 blocks from Fisherman's Wharf. 10 minutes to Pier 39. Plenty of food nearby. Food. The onsite Denny's seems expensive. We had the Lumberjack Slam that we split between 3 ways. It was 2 Pancakes, 2 Eggs, 2 Pieces of Bacon, 2 Sausage Links, Piece of Ham and Hash browns for $13.99. Thats a lot of food, and was perfect for us to split. However Waffles were $11 and Hamburgers were $10+. The first night we were there we ate dinner at the Boudin Bakery on Fisherman's Wharf. I had the Bread Bowl of Chowder and my wife and daughter split a grilled cheese (it was huge  and apparently VERY GOOD). Add a brownie and a bottle of water. Dinner for $20. The second night we went to the Wipe Out Bar and Grill on Pier 39. Standard american food there. Cool atmosphere. Sat outside.Yes parking is expensive, but thanks to Trip Advisor I was prepared for the $88 charge.Must do's. Go to The Stinkin' Rose. Great restaurant with a focus on garlic. Good stuff. Also visit Liguria Bakery (1700 Stockton). Not much of a store but the foccacia bread is outstanding. We got an order of the pizza bread and an order of the raisin bread. Great stuff. Get there early as they run out of stuff as the day goes on. If traveling with children, check out the Aquarium of the Bay at Pier 39. Kids under 3 are free, and adults are $14.95 each.The bad stuff has nothing to do with the city of SF or the Holiday Inn and all to do with Dollar Rental. Terrible. I won't go into all the details here, but it starts with them putting a hold on my check card for the rental, which I know is standard stuff, but they added 15% to the hold and when you are on a budget that extra $120 can go a long ways. I didn't realize this until Friday night. I called the 800 number and was told that I needed to talk to the Customer Service department, which at 8:00 local time was closed for the weekend. Thats helpfull. They said they would release the extra 15% when we returned the car. Which as you could imagine was at the end of our trip and the $120 really didn't do us much good.All in all, we had a great time, and would recommend The Holiday Inn to anyone.

<Author>Pagey54
<Content>Good location for stay in FW We stayed here for 2 nights as the first stop in our self drive Virgin tour. We transfered from the airport , as we picked up the car on day 3, in a $70 pre-ordered limo (I think connected to super shuttles) but it was not there, as promised, and after chasing on the cell phone eventually turned up after a 40 min wait with little apology - maybe best not to prepay or just get a yellow cab from outside of which there seemed to be plenty! The location is ideal, you can walk to any of the major pier's, Ghirardelli square, the cannery, Lombasrd Street and it's on the major bus lines if you want to catch the bus to Golden Gate Bridge. We heard no exterior noise at all, the room was super clean, roomy, comfortable etc as was the bathroom. All the toiletries were stocked when used and towels.We strangely checked in at the main hotel property to then be sent around the corner to a seperate standalone annex with all our luggage. The reception were not exactly friendly, mannerable, or helpful and advised us that the rooms were adjoining, as requested, but when we got there were about 5 rooms apart - it was too much trouble to go all the way back but did not make things easy for us.There is a Denny's below the hotel (we stayed at the Beach st. location) which we used once for breakfast and was ok but we used Joannie's across the road from the main hotel entrance the 2nd morning and had a great brunch there sat outside and was far more reasonable. We ate for the one dinner at Neptunes Palace Restaurant (we pre-booked before leaving the UK) on Pier 39 which had a great panoramic view of the bay, the GG bridge, Alcatrax and a lovely sun set - the food was good but slightly overpriced maybe but no complaints.There is a Starbucks and Walgreens across the street for your late night snack runs and bits and bobs.  If you are going to San Francisco to see the sights this is a place to be and there were other hotels locally that looked just as good. We only had one full day there and pre-booked a combined an all day City bus tour and trip to Alcatraz with Super Sight Seeing Tours (Alcatraz  San Francisco Deluxe City Combo Tour) which was excellent and cost about $70 each. Alcatraz trips can soon sell out so make sure you pre-book to save disappointment.A great city, we fully enjoyed it, although we did not get to see it all.

<Author>Markhan
<Content>Love this Hotel. We have just returned from a 3 week tour of California and used this Hotel for 3 nights at the start and 2 nights at the end. The hotel is in a great location for the piers, ferrys, restaurants and other tourist stuff.As mentioned in previous reviews it is possible to walk into the centre of SF from this location but we cheated and used the Cable car from Hyde St and then The tram system to return.The hotel is very very clean and has everything needed for a great stay but I would recommend eating out elsewhere as both Dennys  Brooklands in the hotel are very overpriced. Street noise was not a problem but I would recommend asking for a room on the 5th Floor business level as this has restricted use by using your room card to access it via the lift.The staff are great at this place and will bend over backwards to make your stay perfect. <Author>PackednReady55
<Content>Location, Location, Location After driving up the Pacific Coast Highway from L.A. and getting into San Fran around 5 PM, we found the Holiday Inn at Fisherman's Wharf to be a welcome stop on our recent vacation. The location is excellent for those that don't mind a little walking. It is only about 2 blocks to Jefferson Street and all the action down at Fisherman's Wharf. The check in was easy and soon we were on our way to our room. Spacious, clean and bright are three words to describe it. Staff was very courteous and more than happy to answer our many questions about the sites in and around the Wharf. One thing about the parking. If you read the Holiday Inn's website, you will see that there is a $39 a day charge. This might seem pricey but it is right there at the hotel. There are parking garages in the area but would be a walk and a question of security. We only stayed one night there but were allowed to park in the parking lot to 6 PM or after. We checked out and loaded up the car with our luggage and then went sight seeing all day without having any concern over our things. It was well worth the money. Overall I would be more than happy to recommend this hotel to anyone visiting the San Francisco area. I will definitely be returning.

The location is ideal, you can walk to any of the major pier's, Ghirardelli square, the cannery and it's on the major bus lines if you want to catch the bus to Golden Gate Bridge. We heard no exterior noise at all, the room was super clean, as was the bathroom. All the toiletries were stocked when used and towel refreshed without issue. The bed was so comfortable that I got a fantastic nights sleep every night -which is unheard of for myself in a strange place. There is a Starbucks and Walgreens across the street for your late night snack runs. There is a very overpriced Denny's in the hotel (we stayed at the Beach st. location) but 2 blocks away is a far more reasonable and better tasting IHOP. If you are relatively fit, you can pretty much walk anywhere in Downtown San Fran, we walked all the way from Union square, thru China town to Lombard st then back to the hotel. The desk staff were very helpful when we were asking about food in the area, with directions and where to go. If you are going to San Francisco to see the sights this is the place to be - Enjoy!!  
<Date>Sep 30, 2008

<Author>SurreyTbt
<Content>nice hotel but steep parking prices put us off Stayed here for 2 nights in Sept with my husband- we stayed in the 2nd building across the street from the main building, which was a bit of a pain for check in and check out as you are lugging your cases across the block, tho it wasn't too far. Couldn't fault the room really, clean, spacious tho air con unit (like many hotels) was pretty noisy and we had to have it turned off at night. Good location for Fish Wharf and for walking to piers that did tours ie Alcatraz (which I would deff recommend). Cab to Union Square was about $15 each way if I remember correctly. There was a store right across from the 2nd building which sold pretty much everything, from toiletries to snacks and water/drinks etc. My main gripe here was the parking charge- we paid $88 for 2 nights, self park, across the block from our building. Just to compare, we only paid $36 in total for 2 nights valet parking in an LA hotel later that week and just $70 for a whole 7 nights self park at a resort in Maui, Hawaii the week after. Way too steep. If I remember correctly, there was a Hertz and an Avis across the street from the 2nd building where we could have picked up a car after our stay in SF for our drive down the PCH to LA. A cab from the airport would have been cheaper than our 2 days car hire and parking charges. Having said that, we drove out of the city to Muir Woods and saw some amazing coastline along the way so we were glad we had the car but you can easily do without one if you are staying in the city.We ate at CheeseCake Factory one night (in Macy's), it was too windy to sit outside but would have been cool to do so if weather was better. Good portions, tasy food etc only downside was that our mains were brought out when we were still in the middle of our starter but would still recommend it and the cheesecake was amazing- we go it to take out.Breakfast at on site Denny's tho convenient and tasty was expensive- $50 with tip for 2 breakfasts and 2 OJ's.I think the parking charges would put me off staying at this place again and it's a shame as there was nothing wrong with the hotel itself- maybe all SF hotels charge excessive parking but if you have a car, look around for other places. If you won't have a car, then this would be a good choice.

<Author>chiswickmum
<Content>hotel is fine - tacky location I was last in SF 20 years ago and loved fisherman's wharf. Returning this year it has turned into a tacky tourist hell hole - there really is nothing appealling about the area though if you want to be surrounded by naff shops, tourist tat and burger restaurants then it could be for you. Granted, it is close to ferries (alcatraz etc) , bike hire, tour buses etc so handy in this respect but I didn't feel comfortable there. The Holiday Inn itself is like any other - clean, efficient and so on but choose your room carefully. This hotel is full of british people on virgin holidays which I didn't like - I wanted to get away from Britain. Unknown to me at booking there are two bulidings, a main one and a satellite called the 'beach' building. It is only staffed in the lobby at peak times which is inconvenient, there is a Dennys in the lobby which stinks the place out and the pool is in the main building which means a 5 minute walk on the main street in your cossie. Get a room looking out onto the courtyard - ours was directly above the main street where trams and taxis woke us up at regular intervals all night - they did move us when we complained. In short - the hotel was fine but its a busy, noisy tourist area so beware.

The major problem is that the Holiday Inn is two separate buildings with no convenient way to commute between them.Most services in the secondary building are usually closed and you really feel isolated. Rooms were nice and large but a bit noisy. Still a great bargain at $135.00. No breakfast is offered and the in building Denny's prices are double the standard rates.Stay away from it and try one of the many small restuarants nearby.This Hotel certainly does not compare to the others in the three star Priceline group and should be dropped to a 2.5 star rating.For the price I would stay there again but would prefer one of the other three star hotels such as Holiday Inn Express, Marriot, Hyatt, Hilton, etc.

<Author>MissCrankyPants
<Content>Perfect location for a first visit. We stayed at this hotel for six nights during a very warm spell and didn't have any problems at all. Our room was on the second floor and had two comfortable double beds and a spacious bathroom. The view was of the road but we were only in the room to sleep so that was irrelevant. I only saw a security guard twice during my stay and didn't come in late enough to discover whether or not the main doors were locked at night. This hotel is within walking distance of so many tourist attractions. Public transportation can take you where your feet can't. We took the #30 bus to see a baseball game without any problems. The bus stop was just across the road! Both cablecar line turn-arounds are within walking distance and the streetcar L-line runs along the wharf. There was a wedding reception and an 18th birthday party held during our stay and we didn't hear any noise at all. <Author>jahlie
<Content>A good value, some problems. We stayed at the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf for two nights for a business meeting and found the room to be just fine. It was clean and we had everything we needed. Our view was the wall next door, but we weren't in the room much and we just kept the curtains closed when we were. That really didn't matter because we've been to San Francisco so often that we've seen the views and weren't particularly interested in one. It's always nice, however. If I had been a tourist seeing San Francisco for the first time, I'd probably want a better view. Wifi is free everywhere in the hotel.The service at the front desk was delightful and helpful. A big problem is that the bar is dark, gloomy and the service surly. We didn't eat breakfast at the restaurant because it is very expensive. Not a fan of the Fisherman's Wharf area, I hopped the street car to the Embarcadero for a Noah's Bagels breakfast sandwich. If you like the area, Denny's is a block away from the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf. There are many other restaurants within an easy walk - 15 minutes to North Beach and 20 to Chinatown. The cable car and street car lines are within a block or two, so getting around is easy. Another problem is that the hotel allows the we're cheaper than the taxi limo scam to take place on their property. Don't ask the doorman to get you a taxi, he'll steer you to the limo - don't fall for it, the limo is always more expensive than a taxi. Just take the taxi waiting on property, call for one, or walk up to the street and one will appear soon. One convenience is that there is a Safeway, Sav On pharmacy and Trader Joe's a couple of blocks up Bay Street. The best shopping is in Union Square or the Embarcadero but again, transportation is easy. I prefer the Embarcadero or Union Square locations in San Francisco but the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf is a good value.  
<Date>Jun 15, 2008

<Author>DisneyDave23
<Content>Great start to our holiday This was destination #1 in our 2007 summer holiday which took in San Francisco (Holiday Inn, Fisherman's Wharf), Yosemite (Yosemite View Lodge), Carmel (Carmel Mission Inn), Santa Maria (Holiday Inn), Beverly Hills (Beverly Hilton), Anaheim (Sheraton Anaheim) and San Diego (Paradise Point). Being a Holiday Inn, it is very err.... Holiday Inn i.e. you know what you are going to get. There is amply parking for guests and as a Virgin guest we were surprised to get it for a third of the usual price without having to ask. Staff are attentive and polite.Rooms are have the solid, corporate feel of a Holiday Inn and are pretty much faultless in that respect. Working desk, free safe and coffee machine are welcome. There is another HI just around the corner with a Denny's diner inside which is handy for breakfast. Out hotel offered breakfast but we hose to explore. There is also a pool but SF in July is not the warmest place to be swimming especially when there is little sun. Overall, no nasty surprises and well recommended. Great price. We are making a return stay in summer 2008.Tip: SF taxis - be very clear with your directions to the driver. The roads can be long and you can get dropped off at the wrong end.Tip: Choose this hotel for easy access in and out especially with a car to outer lying areas,Tip: Fisherman's Wharf can soon feel tiring with all the touristy shops and some of you may well hate it. It is however only a few dollars by cab into the main shopping area. The hotels here are more expensive and car parking starts to become a problem.

<Author>traveluva
<Content>Nice Hotel, Nice Location I booked this hotel through Hotwire for just $62 per night and when I checked their website the same room would have been $200 so I really got a bargain. The rooms are nice, spacious and comfortable. Same with the bathrooms. Usual toiletries, hairdryer and towels are provided and house keeping come once a day. We we initially given a room on the 5th floor which we thought the toilet didnt flush properly and when we complained we were moved instantly. There is a bit of street noise but it is a busy area so you will get that at any time of the day.The location is so convenient. The hotel is literally one block back from the main fishermans wharf. There is a street car stop and a bus stop outside which can take you to Union Square. Pier39 is less than 5 minutes walk.The downside is the cost for parking but everywhere is like that in San Fran and with the location and the public transport you really dont need a car.I enjoyed my stay here. It is a good hotel. I am not sure if it is worth $200 a night but accomodation is not cheap in San Fran and it is comforting to know that it is safe to walk around the area at night as there are some dodgy areas in San Fran.

<Author>brooksy55
<Content>Great Location Before booking my holiday I read Trip Advisor to get an idea of what the hotel was like and thought it seemed okay. Just before we went I looked at the reviews again and got a bit worried, however, I didn't need to be - this was great.We were located in the 2nd building, which is literally just round the corner from the main building, and although there was not anyone on the front desk here, we felt very safe as you need to use your room key to access the lifts.There is a Denny's in the lobby and this proved to be a great help - the first day after arriving we went on a day trip to Yosemite National Park and had to leave at 6am, so with this being open 24 hours, it was ideal for breakfast before we set off.We ended up eating here a few times just because it was so convenient and cheaper than other places around as you are situated in the heart of tourist land!San Francisco itself is great - the Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf area is a bit like Blackpool but if you go up to Pier 39 (about 10 min) walk it鈥檚 much better - still very touristy but much busier and of course home to the famous sea lions.The cable car turn arounds are a few blocks away in either direction and take no more than 10 mins to walk to - we rode the cars just once but it was great to go up and down the hills and see the city this way.Lombard Street is about a 10-15 min walk away - be warned it is up hill all the way, but well worth the walk and the views on the way back down are great.Because we only had a limited time in the city we went on an organised Tour that included a trip to Alcatraz as well as a few hours on a coach being shown the sights of the city. I would recommend doing this as you get to see the major things and we even got to walk across the Golden Gate Bridge. We booked this ourselves via the Internet before we left the UK and had no problems at all. We also used the same company to go to Yosemite on a day trip - although this was a long day, it was well worth it - Yosemite is beautiful.We had a quick dinner in Chinatown at a place called Chef Jai's - this is next door to the famous House of Nanking but without the queues! The look of the place isn't that inviting, but don't be put off - the food is amazing and cheap!Overall the hotel was great - in a really good location. There was a free key operated safe in the room, free internet access in the main building, tea  coffee making facilities in the room as well as a telly and a good sized bathroom. The beds were really comfy, which was just what we needed after an 11 hour flight. The rooms had blackout curtains in them, so you weren't disturbed by sunlight.I would recommend this hotel to anyone who only has a few days to explore the city and wants to be somewhere central as you are really close to everything and the hotel is good value for money.

<Author>Veritas01
<Content>Exceptional Value Booked a room on Hotwire for $79 per night. The hotel is located a block from Fisherman's Wharf. If that part of the city is of interest to you then this hotel is for you. Check in was easy. Parking as everywhere in San Francisco was absurdly expensive. We were charged about $40 per day including tax to park the car in their underground lot. I could not find a good alternative and you really need a car to get to all the attractions especially outside of the city. So I had to bite the bullet. We were put in a building across the street from the main Holiday Inn Building. They called it the Beach Street Buidling as it was on Beach Street. It has a 24 hour Dennys in the lobby and access to the elevators required your key card. The hotel was well maintained and the hallways and public areas were clean. Our room on the 5th floor was roomy and comfortable. Free wifi was a plus. We had two double beds, tv, coffee maker, excellent heating and cooling, great water pressure and hot water, good towels, good housekeeping services, lots of space to store your belongings, a safe for valuable, etc. It is a budget hotel especially if booked on Hotewire or Priceline so you will be with budget seeking people. If you are looking for the upper crust go to the Hyatt. Only drawbacks were I would have liked a fridge and they were asking 9.95 for 24 hours of the Disney Channel. Pretty slimy if you ask me. The hotel was also a bit noisy but a towel at the bottom of the door helped with that. We arrived from New York so Midnight in San Fran was 3 am according to our bodies. Takes a couple of days to adjust. We brought our 9 month old son. The hotel provided a free crib. Metal and very sturdy and clean. Also I used the laundry on the 2nd floor. Two washers and two dryers. 2.00 a load quarters only. 27 minute wash...40 minute drive. Room was immaculate. All in all considering how expensive San Francisco is for just about everything this was a bargain and a great place to stay. If I return I will definitely check this place out again.

<Author>onedude
<Content>Thumbs up Got this on hotwire.com for USD69 a night, arrival 4/4 departure 4/8 (4 nights). We were given a room in the beach tower across the street.I found the quality and standard of this property to be of a very high standard. From the pillow menu, to the individual temperature control, to the free internet, it was an excellent stay in every way. Room was of a good size, bathroom was well laid out, in room safe was free with key, and housekeeping was very effective at keeping everything exceptionally clean.I would like to thank the poster who mentioned the car park at 350 Beach Street. We used this on 3 of our 4 days, and it is an easy 5 minute walk from the hotel. At USD20 a day, it beat paying the USD35 at the hotel. We got free street parking on the Sunday. If you search hard enough, there is free parking on the street down North Point a few blocks, but it is very hard to get. There is also a Safeway a few blocks down which had great pre-made to go sandwiches and cheap alcohol for those looking to save money like us.The only thing that annoyed me about this property was the Denny's in the foyer. They wanted USD12.99 for the Heartland Scramble, which is USD4.10 more expensive than other Denny's in California. Talk about price gauging! Save yourself the money, and walk the two blocks to the iHOP - its a reasonable price, and the quality of the food was exceptional.All in all, an excellent stay in San Francisco, and an excellent stay from Holiday Inn.

<Content>Great Location I stayed at the Holiday Inn during a five day convention in San Francisco. I found this hotel to be quite dated and in need of remodeling. <Author>CheshireBuddie
<Content>Good location for seeing the sights I stayed at the Holiday Inn, Fisherman's Wharf for four nights in October 2007 with three friends on a three centre holiday with Virgin Holidays - San Fransisco first, then on to Las Vegas and Los Angeles. We specifically chose the area of Fisherman's Wharf as it is geared towards the tourist and as we had never visited San Fransisco before, it suited our needs. It's approximately a 20 minute drive from the airport and check in was quick. Virgin Holidays use the second building in the next street but it was only a couple of minutes walk away. The Denny's on the ground floor of our building was really handy and there's a shop and coffee bar in the main hotel foyer. The rooms were very clean and comfortable and also quiet as ours were on the 5th floor. It's only a short walk to the main sights of Fisherman's Wharf and to the cable car turnaround. As it's a busy area, it felt safe at night. We didn't visit the hotel restaurant, preferring to get out and about. Boudin's upstairs restaurant overlooking the sea is worth a visit and there's plenty of choice for food and drink at Pier 39.Our group was extremely satisfied with our stay and if you are looking for a convenient base from which to explore the city, this hotel is an excellent choice in my opinion.

<Author>photog72
<Content>Save on Parking We stayed at this hotel from February 21 and checked out on February 23. Pricelined the hotel for $65 per night. Called ahead and requested a king size bed for just the two of us. When we arrived at the hotel, they granted the request. Based on reviews here, we were put up at the beach hotel - the one with the Denny's inside of it. Our room was an end unit on the second floor. Aside from traffic outside, everything on the inside was just fine. The free wifi was nice to have. I had already reserved a room in the Cow Hollow section of the city. That hotel provided free parking, and cost about $85 per night. So, my goal was to find parking that was less than $35 per night that the Holiday Inn wanted. We found a parking garage close by that has parking for $20 for 24 hours! It is located at 350 Beach St. Look for the Enterprise rental car agency located there too. There was one big negative, you had to prepay your parking. They have automated parking ticket dispensers and I used my credit card to pay for the parking. There are no in/out privileges. You have to park in a numbered stall first, then walk over to the machine and punch in your numbered stall. If you need to take the car out of the garage during the 24 hours, someone else CAN park in that spot, and you'll have to buy more time in another spot. However, if you get back into that spot and you still have the parking ticket, you're golden. Remember to place that parking ticket on top of the dash board so it can be easily viewed. I do not know if access to the garage is granted in the middle of the night, nor what time it closes... if ever. I don't know about security. I do know I kept nothing of value in the car overnight. I do know I saved $15/day by parking there. It is 1 block east (on Beach St.) from the secondary building. Not a far walk at all. When it was time to pack the car for the trip back, I drove it to the temporary parking at the hotel, and we loaded up.

<Author>mochamomBrea
<Content>Not bad We stayed at this hotel, in room 303 (Columbus building), from Dec 23, 2007-Dec 27, 2007. We were given a room with 2 double beds (I thought we'd get queens but you never know with priceline) in the main building of the hotel. The hotel is clean and the staff are helpful. The restaurant inside the hotel, The Bristol, is open for breakfast and dinner, and kids eat free with paying adults. The breakfast prices are high (it can be charged to your room), but cheaper than the Denny's across the street, and a buffet is available; all food was made to order. There is a gift shop inside the hotel where you can purchase souveniers or items you may have forgotten, and even stamps for postcards. Our room was small but clean. The bathroom has a coffee maker (makes a single cup at a time), shampoo, conditioner, soap and lotion. The hotel is located one block from a Starbucks and restaurants, and two blocks from the Cable Car turnaround. Pier 39 is within walking distance. Parking is available, but you have to pay $35 a night plus tax (although we were only charged for one night of parking). There is a concierge on site to provide directions or recommendations for things to do. There is an outdoor pool, and a small exercise room. I also noticed a pool table in the restaurant. While I didn't hate the place, I'd probably stay at a Holiday Inn Express next time because they provide a free breakfast and are newer.

There is no way it deserves a 4. The service was poor. The housekeeping was poor. The look and smell of the hotel was poor. The location was decent, but who cares about that when you are walking around with a sore back all day from the hard beds where I could outline all of the individual springs. I would never recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>M1NX
<Content>Handy for Alcatraz We stayed at this hotel for two nights only.whilst on holiday in the US. Our room was in the Beach building which was a bit of a walk from the main building with our luggage. We didn't try the Dennys partly because of some of the reviews we had read and partly because there was an awful smell from the place. The Beach building was handy for the wharf area and certainly for Alcatraz and Pier 39. Yes the hotel is in a Touristy area, but we are tourists. We ate in Wipeout on pier 39 on our first night, mainly due to the fact that everything seemed to be closing at around 9pm and also that we had just had a very long flight and couldn't be bothered to look too far. The meals were ok but a large budweiser cost $7.95!The hotel room was fine and the room was comfortable and clean.The beds were very comfy.We had a nice view of Alcatraz. Not having been in the main building of the hotel, I couldn't comment on the hotel facilities. We had pre booked our visit to Alcatraz and enjoyed the visit.The views of San Francisco were spectacular from the island. We rode the cable car and walked back through Union Square and China town. We didn't see too many vagrants unlike mentioned in some reviews. But then again we come from a large city and are accustomed to seeing homeless people. On our second night we ate in Lorries diner in Giraldhelli Square. It was fine. The hotel was okay but wasn't worth the price we had paid for it.I think I'd rather go to the Holiday Inn Express next time where breakfast is included. For breakfast on both mornings we ate in the Wharf Coffee House on Beach street.The breakfast was good and the cost reasonable.The staff were so friendly and the coffee shop was near. I would love to return to San Francisco because we didn't have long enough there.

<Author>msstatebulldog
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised Just returned from spending a week at the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf. I decided quite late to attend the Oracle OpenWorld conference. A month before the conference, all hotels in San Francisco were booked. Thanks to a cancellation, I was able to book the Holiday Inn. It wouldn't have been my first choice. I normally stay at a four or five star hotel. Also, this was quite a commute to Moscone.Based on other reviews, I called to request a room in the main building. On arrival, I was given a room on the business executive floor (5th). There were 3 computers available for guests on the floor. My room had free wireless internet, a small refrigerator and microwave. The room had been renovated fairly recently and was in nice shape. The bed was comfortable and with the choices from the pillow menu, I slept surprisingly well.The only downside to the stay was the small in-room safe. I had called in advance to make sure there was a safe in the room that would hold my laptop. I was put on hold for about 5 minutes while they checked. On arrival, I found that the safe was too small to hold my purse, much less my laptop. For the price paid, this was a nice hotel. It is very convenient to the touristy wharf area.

<Author>sangria03
<Content>Nice hotel-good location We went for a midweek getaway for our anniversary from Oct 24-26 2007. Paid $195 a night (AARP rate) for 2 doubles but we got upgraded to a king at checkin. Our room was in thebeach building which was a block away from registration. That was an unexpected walk with luggage We didn't have a car which was a plus as parking is $35 a day. This building has a Denny's restaurant. (one of buildings entrances is the same as the restaurant). Our room on the 6th floor was at the opposited end. (more walking)Room was clean and comfortable. The staff was very friendly. Always a hello when you passed them in the halls. The elevator was friendly too. It would welcome you when entering from the lobby and say goodbye when you got off on your floor. This section of the hotel itself was very quite although our window(which opened) faced a busy street which was noisy quite early in the morning.Room has both wireless  wired internet which was one of the reason we chose it. However I can;' comment on it as we decided to leave the laptop at home at the last minute. Coffemaker was of the heat hot water and instant coffee variety. If you want a good cup of coffee to get you started, thisi isn't it. So while the room was nothing special,the best part of this hotel was the location to public transporation. The Powell-Hyde line cable car line is 2 blocks away and the #30 bus which goes downtown is only a block away. That bus became our best friend and with the vistor muni pass (highly recommended)-took us everywhere we wanted to go.That plus Fishermans wharf a block and 1/2 away make this hotel a good deal and probably the best you will find that close to the wharf.

<Author>Liffey
<Content>Great location We loved the location of this hotel, which is a great selling point. We got put into the annexe, probably because there was an error on our booking (on their part). We didn't mind, but having read other reviews I'd prefer the main building next time. It's a short walk to the annexe and as we had a car in the hotel's car park, a bit of a pain at the end of a long day's sightseeing. We also didn't know you could take the car round to load/unload so we lugged all our stuff there by hand when we first arrived. Someone at the hotel could have helped with that, in hindsight.We wanted the use of a car as we drove out of SF several times, but if you plan to stay in the city don't bother with a hire car. It's $35 a day to park at the hotel and transport is easy in SF with good links near the hotel. The room was clean but the annexe felt a bit quiet and barren. I wouldn't want to be staying there on my own. The lobby isn't always staffed but there was usually a night watchperson around. You can get breakfast (toast etc) at Denny's on the ground floor and take it up to your room (or get a decent husband to fetch it!!) and there was a coffee maker. Being British, I managed to make passable tea with it and the staff at Denny's gave me loads of tiny milk cartons to take to the room. A fridge in the room would have been useful though, to store milk etc. The room could also have done with a couple of easy chairs. We just had one upright chair. All of the staff we encountered were helpful and polite. They got directions for journeys printed off the internet for us.It was an average hotel, no luxuries but adequate for a short stay in SF.

<Author>karleigh04
<Content>Loved the Restaurant  We are a little slow writing this review. We stayed here for four nights and loved the close proximity of this hotel to Fishermans Wharf itself, which is good for any sightseeing around the bay, etc. Our biggest praise though is for the staff and service in the restaurant. They have the best steaks. So so tender and that is saying something when you are from Australia where we have the best steaks. It was my birthday whilst staying here and the manager and staff of the restaurant made it really enjoyable for me, arranging for some cakes and even singing happy birthday. My daughter also enjoyed having internet access and I enjoyed finally having laundry facilities which were sadly lacking in our other accommodation choices on the west coast. All in all we would recommend this hotel and would not hesitate to stay here again.

<Author>lindenCR
<Content>Ehhhh...so-so stay at the Holiday Inn As all the other reviews state, location, location, location....nothing here wowed us over our 3 night stay except the easy walk to Fishermans Wharf. I thought for $245/night (AAA rate) the room was a little small for our family of 4....bathroom was decent, shower pretty good and all were very clean. No fridge is a HUGE incovenience with kids...had to ask for extra ice buckets to keep a few drinks handy and cold. Ate one meal at the restaurant in the main building where we stayed...DO NOT recommend it! Kids eat free (meals for them were pretty good), but not a lot of selection for us grownups and the prices are outrageous! (Doesn't even make up for the fact that the kids meals are free!) Can't comment much on the service...didn't really need anything during our stay. Parking is pretty steep, but seems on par with everything else in the area. We never got a chance to use the pool (weather was very cold, rainy and windy), but it looked ok. Overall, doubt we'll be back to San Francisco anytime soon, but would probably chance another hotel next time anyway.

<Content>NOT a 3 Star Hotel! We were in a room in the annex, down the street and around the corner. There was no desk clerk in that building. <Author>WXRN
<Content>Great Location, but That's It. This is a great location. It is an easy walk to Fisherman's Wharf, the cable cars, Ghiardelli Chocolate, and even the Alcatraz Tour, though that was a bit further. Parking was $35 per night, but what can you do. The main lobby was very nice, but we got stuck in the building next door, which I believe is where all the riff-raff with AAA discounts are condemned. There is no parking there, except for around 10 spots near the main entrance which were constantly full. So, you have to double park, drop off the luggage, then drive back to the posh hotel to park. Then you repeat the process when you leave. The annex is barren, except for the Denny's, which was crowded (not sure why with so much great food around). The rooms were adequate and clean. We only got 3 bath towels for the 4 of us, and it took over an hour on two consecutive nights to get a 4th. Our view was of the tourists in the next wing of the annex. We would stay again only for the location, but try to get a room in the main building. Maybe things are nicer there.

<Author>busymakingwings
<Content>Great location, very helpful staff Stayed for 4 nights at the end of a 17 day vacation in California. The hotel staff are very professional and helpful. As we used our Priority Club membership number when we booked (even though we have only used it once before) we were given an excellent room exclusive to club members and given tokens for two free drinks in the bar. Nice touch we thought. Also on our floor there were three PC's available so we could use the internet free of charge.The room had a great view over to Alcatraz (albeit with a sub view of the car park next to the hotel). The room was spacious, clean with nice toiletries and a bath robe. Also there was good information in the room about what to do in San Francisco.We ate out for breakfast most days and found a great diner in Ghiradelli Square which was excellent - great food and service.We did use the bar on one or two evenings as we met up with friends travelling from Australia and the kids especially enjoyed the Pool Table. One negative point. One of the female bar staff on duty was really miserable and kept telling us the kids were not allowed to drink which we were well aware of and had ordered them soft drinks anyway.Nice swimming pool and fitness room which was an added bonus.The doormen were exceptional. Always helpful and their service was excellent. With our friends we were a party of six and thought we would hire two taxis to take us to the Golden Gate Bridge but the doorman suggested hiring a limo for an hour as it would work out cheaper. It was a great idea as we not only got to see the bridge, we drove over it, he stopped both ends to allow us to take prictures then also drove us to Lombard Street afterwards. Great value for $75.Tip if you want to go to Alcatraz and they do not have a time slot for you. Show up at 8.00 and you will have a great chance of getting on a trip as they receive unused bookings back overnight. We were told the earliest was on the next Tuesday, the day we were leaving so we thought we wouldn't be able to go. We heard about going down to the ticket office at 8.a.m. on the Monday and got on the 9.a.m. boat no trouble at all. Well worth the visit too.Fisherman's Wharf is just around the corner. It is very busy but great fun for a few days. The cable car is two minutes away also so it is easy to get around the city yet we found our room to be very quiet and relaxing.The hotel booked us a shuttle back to the airport on the day we left.Overall we had a great few days. Good value, good location and aexcellent service.

<Author>SmithS&B
<Content>Staff need to go on customer service training! We stayed in the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf for 4 nights in June 2007. Upon arriving we were shown to our room in the Annexe building. No bar, no restaurant (just a Dennys) no receptionist. The room was fine but it over looked the dumpsters at the back and faced a brick wall. Not ideal but we thought it would just have to do. At 6 am the next morning we got an unscheduled alarm call as the truck arrived to empty the dumpsters. The noise was so horrendous it felt like the truck was actually reversing through our bedroom. An hour later when we had just managed to get back to sleep the truck arrived back to empty more dumpsters!We went down to request that we be moved to another room and the receptionist was very frosty. Muttered a lot about if we didnt like that room then we would like this one etc. I finally lost my temper and yelled at her we have had this trip booked for 6 months and flown half way across the world. There is no way you are putting us in a crappy room in an annexe that you only give to someone when there is nothing left. All of a sudden there is a room available in the main building over looking the pool, Ideal! It was a nice room, no noise at all. The concierge was completely off-hand when we asked him to book transfers to the airport and actually snatched our flight details out of my husband's hand. The reception staff were very unhelpful when we told them we had a problem with our bill. To top it all our airport transfer that the concierge arranged was late. We decided to save time and use the auto check in terminal they have in reception. We went through the check in procedure and the boarding cards did not print out. We explained this at reception and their answer was oh, that's not working. (They knew it wasn't working but did not think to put a sign on it saying so) We then had a job trying to explain at the airport why we had checked in but had no boarding cards. The whole place was extremely unprofessional and the staff had a couldn't care less attitude. On the plus side, the room was OK and clean and location good for Fisherman's Wharf and the Cable Car to Union Square.Would not stay here again. We had spent the previous week in Las Vegas where the customer service we experienced was first class every place we went. We were firmly disappointed with the Hol Inn.

<Author>SJB100
<Content>Satisfactory hotel, excellent location I stayed at the Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf for three nights at the end of April 2007.I stayed in the hotel block which was located around the corner from the main hotel. For me this caused no problems. I found the staff polite and friendly. They were happy to take my luggage to and from the main building where I got dropped off and picked up. I would recommend this hotel and would stay there again myself. If you find yourself staying in the hotel block around the corner it really is only a few minutes walk and had no impact on my stay whatsoever.

The word 鈥楢nnex鈥?conveys the impression of something tacked on and 鈥榰pgrade鈥?of unexpected benefits and luxury. When we got to the room, I couldn鈥檛 help but think 鈥渋f this is the upgrade, then I wonder what the standard rooms are like鈥? I wouldn鈥檛 go as far as to say it was awful, but it was certainly very tired and in desperate need of refurbishment. It also had a hint of that nasty odour caused by stale cigarette smoke which I suppose was not unexpected. In short, it was disappointing. If it wasn鈥檛 for the fact we were cross eyed with tiredness coupled with the knowledge we were only there for one night, I would probably have requested a different room. On the cleanliness front, I would describe it as reasonably clean but not spotlessly clean. With regard to the heating/air conditioning arrangements, there did not seem to be much variance between hot and cold on the rather ancient unit. Fortunately, neither was really necessary; we had excellent weather for January. On the positive side, there was complimentary internet access on the floor (part of the 鈥榰pgrade鈥?package), as well as a decent sized fridge in the room. We found the staff to be helpful and pleasant, particularly the concierge. We didn鈥檛 eat in the hotel; breakfast seemed expensive for what it was, but there were a number of places just a few minutes walk away from the hotel that did breakfasts for just a few dollars. For dinner, I had done a little bit of research before we arrived. Seemed to me that while there were indeed loads of restaurants in the vicinity, none seemed to stand out as being particularly remarkable. So we picked out one in the Russian Hill district called Antica Trattoria on Polk Street (at Union). It is a 鈥榥eighbourhood鈥?restaurant (ie frequented by locals) 鈥?always a good sign in my experience. It was excellent (you can look it up by tapping the name into Google). Overall though we found the area to be quite pleasant with a relaxed atmosphere; the nearby Cannery certainly falls into that category. From that perspective, the hotel is very well located. <Author>welshgirlinessex
<Content>Distinctly average OK, so we came here after a stay in Vegas (Venetian) and Hawaii (Hilton) which are very nice hotels - we weren't expecting top class service being a HI but we expected more. When we checked in, they could barely be bothered and gave us a tired looking twin. No help was offered with our 3 large suitcases. I went back downstairs to ask for a king room and they upgraded us to the 5th which was marginally better (never used the microwave) but we weren't told we had to use the room key to get on the 5th floor . We liked the internet access. The rooms were clean and functional. We went downstairs to get a drink and something to eat (about 9.45) - the restaurant was closed (it was supposed to close at 10) so we asked the bartender for a bar menu. He gestured towards the drink menu and we had to repeat our request. He virtually tutted and got a grubby sheet of A4 paper out with about 4 or 5 things on it (calamari, fries, a sandwich - not an inspiring choice). We'd been travelling for hours so we ordered some food and a couple of beers. After another beer, we ordered a Baileys - he asked how we liked it and I told him 'on the rocks' - he then had the nerve to tell me off that 'over here you have to tell us how you want it'. As someone who has travelled extensively in the US (and have never had any problems anywhere else!!) I found him patronising and rude to us (particularly when some other guests came in, we could barely get him to serve us - despite our legendary British politeness!). When we were due to leave, we asked the concierge to book us an airport shuttle - he told us that we could pay later. Thinking he'd booked it, we went for breakfast and checked out. He then told us he hadn't booked it for us and the next one wasn't for 30m mins (luckily we had plenty of time) but it was the attitude that was appalling. I wished I'd stuck to my guns and not let our travel agent talk us out of the Westin now - I was ready to pack my things and pay extra to stay there insteadRecommendations  - the Buena Vista for breakfast and great views of the bay- book Alcatraz in the UK on the internet- go and see the sealions on Pier 39- stay up at Union and not at Fisherman's Wharf- take a coat (we had to buy one)- don't go in November - go to the Stinking Rose - fabulous meal

<Author>visit_world
<Content>Good accomadations at a Descent location We stayed Oct 11 to the 14th. Got a great deal from Priceline and I wouldn't bay over $110 for this hotel room. We payed much less than this though...The Holiday Inn Fisherman's Warf is a 3.5 star hotel in my opinion. We stayed three nights in one of the adjacent buildings right above the Denny's. The room was well kept, new looking, and the housekeeping was the friendliest. The bed was very comfy and the bathroom was clean and looked new. The carpet and all the room decor was excellent.The bad thing about this hotel is the parking cost. $35 a night is way too much. You would think they would charge $20 a night, which I think is reasonable. I suggest parking in the streets nearby or in the other parking lots. The other perk of this hotel is that it is 5 min walk to Pier 39 and 1 min away from Fisherman's Warf. The other advantage is that the bus and F-line (which takes you into Union square) is right outside. great location.Other hints:1. Do not eat in the Denny's. It is so so expensive. Walk down the street to the IHOP for half the price and better quality and quantity. 2. Walk over to Lombard street (crooked street). Great to see.3. Ask hotel concierge for assistance. They are great.4. Hotel lobby is not impressive and breakfast buffet didn't look worth it. Best to eat at IHOP!5. Don't take the cabs into Union square. Take the BUS (30). It gets you there in 10-15 mins. Also you can take the trolley car which is only a block away on HYDE. Both my wife and I enjoyed our stay here and we would highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>Heavens
<Content>3rd Stay's not the charm! We had stayed here 3 times before and decided to stay here again as the location was fantastic and we had good experiences with the hotel.This stay was not to be as enjoyable as previous stays! We booked this stay some time ago with Virgin Holidays and were relay excited to be back in San Francisco again!On arriving we checked in. The Holiday Inn is spread across 2buildings, a block apart. A main building and their 2nd building onBeach Street. We were checked into a double room in the other building.We asked if we could stay in the main building and said that we wouldprefer a King Size bed as we were on an anniversary trip. The manager advised us that this was not possible but the room he had allocated us was a lovely room and we should not be disappointed. He said that all their Virgin Holidays customers were always put up in the 2nd building (which was strange as we had always booked with Virgin and had always stayed in the main building!). He advised that we would need to go to the other building and showed us on a map where it was and where the room was.There was no offer of a bell, and the bell men merely just watched us as we dragged our 2 oversized cases, cabin luggage and rucksack across the 1 block hike to the other hotel.We arrived at our room and opened our curtains to find that we werelooking out at a brick wall and we were above the dumpsters and service entry. We were so angry at this having been told that our room would be 'lovely' we went straight downstairs to talk to someone at reception.The reception in the second building was closed (this was approx 3pm ~ normal check in time) and there was no concierge on duty either. We had to walk over to the main building to actually speak with someone!We got to the main building and spoke with another desk staff employee.We advised them of how dissatisfied we were with our room and that wewanted to change. He advised that he would not be able to change us as there were no rooms available as yet. We asked if any were likely to come available and he was unable to answer as they were unable to view all the rooms! After a few moments he said he had located one in the main building and it was a much better room. He said we would need to move from the other building. Again no offer of a bell or even when we walked past the bell (Bear in mind they were VERY busy in conversation with each other!).So we returned to the 2nd building and got all our luggage together and dragged it all back to the Main building and found our new room. Our new dark room! We were looking straight out at a brick wall and still no king size bed as requested!Back to the reception desk again where we spoke with the most venomous woman I have had the displeasure of dealing with! We explained that we were unhappy with the rooms we had been given and wanted a new room. To this we were patronised and spoken down to. She said that we should never have been moved to the main building as it was not policy to have Virgin holiday customers in the main building ~ they are all put up in the 2nd building. We explained that we did not want to stay in the 2nd building and would prefer the main building. We also explained that we had previously booked with Virgin and had always stayed in the main building. This woman then made out that we were lying and said there was nothing much that she could do. Bear in mind that while all this is going on she is wearing a badge that says 'It's all about YOU'!! What a joke.After some time she starts looking at rooms muttering 'If you weren'thappy with that then you won't be happy with this one'. In less that 10 minutes this woman had gotten to know us so well that she knew what me and my husband would like! She tried to move us back to our original room (the one overlooking the dumpster) to which we refused and she finally found us a room in the main building. Again we had to move your own luggage to a room that was one floor higher than our previous room and overlooked the same brick wall!At this point we were exhausted from our transatlantic flight and theluggage moving we had been doing! We decided to settle as it appeared that Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf was no longer 'All About YOU!'After the worst night sleep ever (the room was over the garbage andservice entry on the main building) we decided to try the reception desk one last try to see if any rooms had become vacant during the morning.We spoke to a FANTASTIC lady (Remi) who was very sympathetic to ourneeds and searched out a room for us. She found one which was stillbeing cleaned but put a rush on it for us. Everything that the previous days staff said wasn't possible was suddenly very possible! We were in our new room within the hour! Remi also offered to have our luggage moved for us ~ something that we hadn't been offered before either!Our new room was great ~ Remi had upgraded us to the 5th floor (the only real difference in the actual room is you get a microwave). But we were high enough up not to hear any of the service lorry noises and we actually had a view of the city!We went along to our 'Virgin holidays Rep' meeting and spoke with other holiday travellers there. And what a surprise, most of these were in the main building. So this so called policy of putting Virgin Customers in the 2nd building seems a bit suspect to me.Our stay was fantastic after Remi sorted things out for us. We nearly cancelled our stay and moved across the street due to the previous nights farce at reception!If you are a Virgin Holidays customer, and are staying for 4nights ormore, make sure you attend the welcome meeting and get your FREE BayCruise (worth $21 dollars each). The Virgin rep does not like to give these out unless he is pressed!Would I stay here again - No! One bad experience at check in has ruined 5 years good work by this hotel!

<Author>Dinolola
<Content>Tourist conveyor belt in awful location This hotel is probably one of the worst we have ever stayed in. When checking in the receptionist probably wouldn't have even noticed if our heads were on upside down. We were not told where the room was, never mind about any of the amenities or breakfast times etc. Our room was cold, dark and overlooked a blank blue wall. In the morning we discovered that we were situated next to the hotel loading area and the noise from the trucks reversing was horrendous. We asked to change rooms, which was an incovenience not just for us, but by the response from the staff was also and inconvenience for them as well. We were offered an upgrade to a business room at an additional charge of $40 per night but the room was the same apart from the fact it had a microwave oven (??) so we declined. In the end we were offered a room overlooking the street and pool area which at least made the room brighter and appear warmer. The rooms were clean, and functional but nothing special. A bit dated and drab but I suppose it was just a 'base' at the end of the day. Don't be expecting anything luxurious, this hotel is just functional and sees tourists come and go like a conveyor belt. Fishermans Wharf was not our cup of tea, but everybody likes different things. We found it very tacky (Blackpool), lots of gift shops selling junk, arcades and the usual attractions as seen in Blackpool - Ripleys Belive It Or Not  the obligatory wax museum etc. Restaurants sell lots of seafood, clam chowder is inescapable. Great bakery (Boudin sourdough) worth a visit and the seals on Pier 39 are great. Lots of homeless people and gangs of lads on the corner make it feel a little unsafe, especially at night. The best places to hang out at the Wharf were Ghiradelli Square and the Cannery - more sophisticated. The Mandarin chinese restaurant at Ghiradelli is EXCELLENT. Also recommend a visit to North Beach area as well with some good italian eateries. Union Square has LOTS of homeless. We have never experienced it on such a scale before. It is very sad seeing all these poor people in a country so full of obvious wealth, you really had to have your witts about you as sometimes it can be a bit scary. Also recommended HIGHLY is trip to Alcatraz. TIP - Take plenty of fly spray - the island is infested with the little beggars. We had a nice time but will not ever be returning to the Holiday Inn.  
<Date>Oct 15, 2006

<Author>Tubster
<Content>OK, but didn't like the area Stayed 3 nights here in a room in the Beach St site. A few blocks down to Ghiradelli Square, a block down to the main street fronting the wharf and Pier 39 an easy stroll of around 15-20 mins. We had requested a room with 2 doubles, and on checking in requested a rollaway be put in the room. By the time we had crossed the street from reception, the boy from housekeeping was waiting at the door with the rollaway. Unfortunately, when we entered the room, water was coming through the ceiling, so we had to cross back over to reception to request a room change. This was done efficiently and promptly. It was a bit of a squeeze with the rollaway, but with only being there 3 nights, it wasn't a problem.. Two of our party wanted to go to see the 49's football game, and the concierge, Ryan, could not do enough to help sort out tickets, and advice with transport.Overall, handy location for the Wharf, cable cars  trolleys. Hertz, Avis rentals, one minute walk . Clean rooms, comfortable beds, staff we came into contact with, all polite  professional. All in all, hotel was o.k, but would not stay here again as we disliked the Wharf area.If you are thinking of riding a bike over the Bridge, be careful if you are not a keen cyclist. The info leaflet said there was one small incline. From Fort Mason you have to climb a double incline, very steep ( everyone we saw were pushing their bikes up) without a cycle path - you share the road with the traffic. I am not saying this to put anyone off, just to let people be aware before they book. We made it ,and bought the t-shirt!

<Author>pixandbee
<Content>Honeymoon We stayed at the Holiday Inn, Fishermans Wharf on the second week of our honeymoon - first week of July '06. We had spent the first week in Las Vegas in heat of 108 degrees! Although we had been warned it would be cooler in SF, the jackets we had with us were not enough, so had to buy jackets from stall across the road straight away! We had luckily booked our Alcatraz tour tickets on the Internet in the UK because they were fully booked for the next three days! Book before you leave UK! The Holiday Inn was fine. Nothing to shout about, but perfectly adequate for our needs. We stayed in the room one night and had room service and the meal was lovely. We did notice that the staff at check in were a bit slow..... Didnt use Dennys downstairs at all. Went out for breakfast - our favourite was Johny Rocket's. Happy Days style diner, complete with jukeboxes on the tables. Also had very good breakfasts at restaurant across the street from the main building on Columbus. Ate loads of seafood - Crab House on Pier 39 was good on our last night, if a little bit expensive - although we did have champagne! The Stinking Rose restaurant was excellent - even if we did reek of garlic for the next two days! The Comedy club at the Cannery was good fun. Caught ferry over to Sausalito on last day - foggy and cold in SF but sunny and hot over there - great place for shopping ladies! Yes, Fishermans Wharf is a bit tacky, but can also be amusing (look out for the Bush Man) and the Holiday Inn is well positioned for the F line MUNI trolley bus and the cable cars. Make sure you get a City Pass - excellent value for buses, trolleys and cable cars for 7 days. Had a lovely time - thanks SF!

<Author>terriraven
<Content>great location We (2 adults, 2 children ages 10y, 15y) stayed for 4 nights on the 5th floor. We had to use our key card in a special slot on the elevator in order to get to this floor. There were 2 computers and printers on the floor (also on other floors) with free internet access. ROOM: 2 double beds; mattresses a little too soft (perhaps old?) and our backs were sore in the AM. There was a TV, microwsave and refrigerator. Roomy, clean and comfortable. The view: looking at the beautiful houses on the hill and overlooking the pool. Highly recommend getting a room on this side of the hotel (North Pointe St.) instead of asking for Bay view-you can't really see too much bay and mostly buildings. Bathroom: clean, ok size. We were able to park our car in the underground garage and gain access to it at any time. The best part: when we checked out, we could still keep our car in the garage until 6pm. We are an active family who walks everywhere in SF 95% of the time and enjoyed being so close to the wharf, Nob Hill, China Town, North Beach (great Itlalian cafes), the churches, Coit Tower, and the Embarcadero. Watched firewords at the beach and it was nice to be able to walk a short distance back to our room. Everyone was very pleasant and had a quick ck-in and ck-out. There's an ok restaurant downstairs, but service is questionable-saw our waitress once when ordering and then sat around waiting for the ck after we finished. Recommend Pergarino's across the street. Cable cars are close by. The only drawback was in the early AM hrs, we could clearly hear the delivery trucks, garbage trucks, etc. Good part: did not hear any neighbors at any time. Pool: on the cool side. Overall, I would recommend this hotel. Good for the price and yes, we would return.

<Author>Karen008
<Content>Comfortable Hotel Hotel was located close to Fisherman's Wharf and the Cable Cars.We had a really nice stay at the hotel. If you join the Priority Club, you get some nice privileges - just go to the Holiday Inn website and sign up.There was a Walgreen's close by which was really convenient - there was a Starbucks nearby also where you can sit and watch the streetcars come in. Cable Cars are a fun way to get around town. We bought the CityPass which was a good deal. It has a 7 day Muni Pass which gives unlimited rides on Cable Cars, Buses, and Street Cars. There are restaurants near the Holiday Inn. There's a good pizza place across the Street. Pier 39 is also close by. Fisherman's Wharf has the Rain Forrest Cafe and Boudin. We decided to go to Chinatown for many of our meals. Great Eastern restaurant on Jackson Street was excellent. Holiday Inn was very comfortable. It was clean and the staff were friendly. You can buy Mrs Fields cookies in the lobby after 5pm.

<Author>gingerwife
<Content>Awful - don't stay here! Two things: firstly, Fisherman's Wharf is a really bad location to stay in, in San Francisco - none of the best restaurants are in the immediate area, and Fisherman's Wharf itself is a tacky tourist trap (even San Fran residents are embarassed about it). Secondly, if you must stay here, the Holiday Inn is dire and should be avoided. On arrival, we were given a room in the beach block (which is a 5 minute walk from reception and nowhere near the waterfront!). The room was already occupied and someone's clothes were sill in the room. On our second attempt, the room we were given was dark, gloomy, a little shabby and overlooked the carpark - albeit it had a large TV and clean bathroom. The swimming pool is small and next to the main road - not worth booking the hotel for this perk. When we checked out, it took a twenty minute wait as the reception staff were clearly overworked and underpaid.Food: the main eating place in the Holiday Inn is a Denny's - a real crime to eat in this chain when there are so many excellent one-off places throughout the city (e.g. Mama's near Washington Square for brunch, Tomasso's in the North Beach for dinner). There was nothing more depressing than walking past a load of overweight people shovelling processed meat into their mouths every morning. I guess they couldn't be bothered to walk to the better places, as there are none in the immediate area.In terms of location, the Holiday Inn is convenient for the boats to Alcatraz - but that's about it. You are better off staying in the Nob Hill/Russian Hill area which is much closer to good restaurants, the Haight, Castro, Union Square, Golden Gate Park, the Ferry Building etc. We also stayed in the Carlton Hotel during our vacation, and this was excellent value - nicely decorated room, friendly and efficient staff, convenient location - and most importantly - no Denny's!

<Author>margarita2
<Content>Loved The Holiday Inn at Fishermans Wharf We stayed at The Holiday Inn at Fishermans Wharf for 3 nights at the end of April 2006. This was our first stop on our tour of California. We had flown all the way over from the UK and was absolutely exhausted when we arrived. We were greated by a friendly Bell Boy once entering the main reception and were checked in by a helpful and friendly receptionist. We were told that we were in the Annex building on Beach Street which is just opposite. (It would appear that the Brits package holidaymakers are put in the annex building - we booked through Virgin). The building hads a 24 hr Dennys restaurant on the ground floor and it also has a reception area, however it wasn't always manned when we were there. The Denny's restaurant is really handy, and the staff very polite and courteous. It was a little more expensive than the other Denny's restaurants that we have used, but the food and service was excellent. Our hotel room was in very good/ clean order and it would appear that it was newly refurbished. The carpet was like new and the general decor in very good order. There is a in room safe, iron and Ironing board and tea making facilities provided in the room. In the main building, there is a little gift shop, coffee bar, restaurant and bar. It is also very well located to Pier 39, and the restaurants and shops etc locally. This is a all round excellent hotel, and would definately stay here again.

<Content>Great Location We stayed for 3 nights as part of a 2 week holiday in America to celebrate our 25th Wedding Anniversary. After staying in other hotels during our holiday the Holiday Inn provided better in room facilities than the Hyatt in Hawaii, Millenium Biltmore in LA or our theme hotel in Las Vegas. It feels a safe area and we were comfortable walking around day or night. I found the concierge helpull and the staff friendly, i would stay there again You don't go to San Francisco and spend loads of time in your room, it's a great City with loads of places to go. The cable cars are great fun and the walk along the Golden Gate bridge a must.

<Content>Loved it! My Husband, and I stayed at The Holiday Inn, Thursday, Jan 19th, because I had a seminar to go to in the Hotel the next day. When we arrived we only had to wait a couple of minutes, and we were checked in by a very friendly, lovely, girl, who was very helpful. I was worried because of some of the reviews on this Hotel. I had nothing to worry about. My husband parked our car in the Hotel garage, and we went to our room on the 5th floor. It was a lovely room, which also had a large desk for me to do my work.It had a refridgerator, microwave,T.V., large comfortable chair with ottoman,and the room was big,, with a lovely bathroom, which had a make-up mirror. We were also given a late checkout for 4pm the next day. That was great, because of the seminar I had to go to.Our room looked up onto a hill, with homes and over to the financial district where we could see the Pyramid building. It was very quiet, and we could also see the pool from our room. The gym was small, but my husband enjoyed it. I had signed up to be a priority member, (it's free) and was issued a card for two free drinks in their Bristol Bar and Restaurant, and our dinner was excellent. Especially, the cream of Asparagus soup. My husband had salmon, which was very fresh, I had lamb, which was excellent. But, the best thing was the double chocolate mouse cake. Ghiradeli Square is two blocks, and the Wharf is two blocks away also. I will definetly stay here again. There was even a note in our room, that read,if you are not satisfied with something, please call the manager so we can make it right for you. They went out of their way to make our stay a great one.
