<Author>TVTravel
<Content>Avoid this place! When I attempted to check in at the Holiday Inn, two desk clerks were attempting to help a large group of German tourists. I stepped into the Priority Club line, in back of one other person checking in, expecting to be assisted next. WRONG! Instead, two of the desk clerks disappeared entirely, leaving one poor soul to deal with everyone. After 15 minutes, there was no sign of the others coming back and there were still at least eight people in line. The one desk clerk said she would not be able to assist me in the Priority Club line, and said I should join the other line. (Why offer Priority Club check in if you don't want people to use it?) Needless to say, that meant I was now in back of not only the German Tourists (asking tons of questions and making the process very slow), but everyone else who had joined that line in the interim. I decided that at this rate it would take at least another 30 minutes, so I went to dinner instead of waiting.When I returned, there was still only one desk clerk, so I got in line about 4 people back. The line advanced slowly and eventually I reached the front just in time to have an entire airline flight crew show up and enter at the flight crew only line. Needless to say, the desk clerk abandoned me and checked them in first. She eventually returned without apology and I got my room key. Overall time checking in: in excess of 60 minutes!My room at the Holiday Inn was satisfactory in a standard hotel sort of way - nothing special. It fronted on an air space. Since the Fishermans Wharf area is quite noisy, the lack of a street view was no loss. In addition to the 24 hour lobby Denny's Restaurant (as a chain, best to avoid) the hotel offers a coffee bar with fresh juice, fruits, and cereals which was the best thing about the entire hotel. Like all San Francisco hotels, they gouge you on parking ($30/day), so be sure to allow for that fee in your budgeting process.I frequently travel to San Francisco on business. Since my clients are walking distance to Fishermans Wharf, I always stay in that area even though it is obviously touristy. I've stayed at the Hyatt, the Best Western, and the Holiday Inn Express on previous visits. None are perfect, but all are better than the Holiday Inn. Since Holiday Inn's Priority Club seems to be the only frequent stayer program that actually lets you use the awards you've earned, I favor those hotels. On my next trip, I'll probably go back to the Holiday Inn Express, which is the same price as the Holiday Inn, but has more reliable hotel-wide wireless internet and a complimentary continental breakfast.

<Author>UK_ANON
<Content>Average hotel, great location for seeing San Fran We stayed at this hotel for four nights in late September. Our room was on the executive floor and had view of Alcatraz in the distance. The room was comfortable, with queen beds and a microwave. However, the room could have been better cleaned, and it was not double glazed, so there was a certain amount of noise from air conditioning units and the road (despite being on the fifth floor).We did not eat at the hotel, mainly because the restaurant was expensive and always empty. We had vouchers for free tea/coffee at breakfast time. When we tried to redeem these, we were told that they only had fruit tea, and a limited selection of pastries. These were not significant issues due to the location, which had numerous other alternatives nearby.The location of the hotel is excellent. It is approximately five minute walk from fishermans wharf, pier 39, the cable car terminal and very near to a tram stop. In the evenings the location allowed us a great variety of restaurants within a short walk. It was possible to reach China Town, Little Italy, and a range of seafood restaurants on the bay.The parking at the hotel was $32 + tax per day. This was expensive, but expected in a good location in a big city. On the fifth floor corridor there were a couple of PCs with free Internet access.

<Author>brian_lorraine
<Content>Good location, awful service, and expensive I spent 2 nights at Holiday Inn Fisherman's Wharf last week, the last 2 days of a roadtrip that took me to a handful of similar Holiday Inn properties.Our room rate of $196.00 midweek was expensive, so I was expecting reasonable service and a comfortable room. In reality, the room and the service level was significantly worse than at a $60 Holiday Inn Express in other cities.The first (non-smoking) room that we were given - as Gold-level priority club members - was tatty and stank of smoke, and looked out onto a bank of noisy air-conditioning units. We immediately asked to be moved to a cleaner, quieter room, which we were given. There was nothing wrong with the room, but it looked a bit worn and tired, and really was nothing special at all.Front-desk staff were arrogant, curt, and verging on rude. We used some $10 restaurant vouchers we had to have breakfast in the hotel, which was a mistake! We were sat at a table and offered coffee, and all of the coffee cups were dirty - they had 1/2 of milky brown water in the bottom, and bits of food stuck around the mug as if they'd been rinsed off in dirty water. The cutlery was the same - my fork had a bit of dried egg inbetween the prongs!Anyway, we ordered our breakfast, waited 25 minutes, and eventually 3 of our 4 breakfasts arrived. My omlette didn't. I could see the waitress standing by the kitchen door chatting to another member of staff. I waited and waited, and eventually asked for the manager who came and apologised, and my omlette turned up about 5 minutes later, by which time the rest of my family had finished and was ready to leave.Breakfast for 4 of us - which was 4 coffees and 4 omlettes / eggs  bacon etc - came to $80, the biggest rip-off and the worst service that I have every experienced in any hotel. Fortunately, the manager took $40 off after I'd complained about the service.Parking at the hotel is perfectly ok, but at $32.00 + tax per day it isn't cheap. I noticed that there were some public parking lots near the cruise ship terminal for $10 a day which would have been a better bet.All in all, the hotel was poor value for money. Overpriced, complacent, and poorly-trained staff. Our total bill for 2 nights' accomodation, tax and parking (without the breakfast) came to almost $600. The next night we stayed in a Holiday Inn Express near the airport for $69.00 which was twice as good.

<Author>U2fan
<Content>Great location... but noisy! We stayed in this hotel for three nights en-route from Hawaii to the UK. We were located on the 3rd floor in the annex building. The room was spacious and comfortable, and our bathroom was huge! We got a free newspaper delivered every morning. The best thing about this hotel is it's location - it's opposite Fisherman's Wharf and all the attractions around the bay, e.g. Ghiardelli Square, Pier 39, tourist ferries around the bay / Alcatraz, etc. We walked to Lombard Street (up an impossibly steep hill) and back in approx. half an hour. The terminus of the 'F line' tram to the Ferry Building / Market Street (where all the main shops are) / Castro district was literally across the road - it's only $1.50 each, which includes a free transfer within 90 minutes. The terminus of the Powell / Hyde cable car was also only a few minutes walk (I'd recommend getting there early to avoid the queues. We got there at 9.30am and got straight on. It's expensive though - $5 each per journey.) The only downside to the hotel was the noise from the street. My advice if you're staying here is to ask for a quiet room (there were some rooms overlooking a central 'courtyard', which may have been quieter) or bring earplugs! We also encountered lots of noise from hotel staff, e.g. banging doors, so don't expect a lie-in!

<Author>deelar
<Content>Excellent Location We stayed at the hotel for three nights. We upgraded to the 5th floor (Exec level) and would recommend this to others. The room was immaculate and tastefully decorated. Maid service was prompt and thorough each day. Bathroom is small but well equipped and attractively decorated.The staff was helpful and pleasant, except for the concierge. He was on duty each morning we were there, but chose not to be helpful the two mornings we asked him a question. Both days he handed us a map and a look that clearly said you're grown ups, figure it out for yourself. So, unless you want a map you can give him a miss.If you're visiting San Francisco to enjoy the sites, this is a super hotel to choose.During your trip, consider visiting Alcatraz--it's quite an experience for young and old. The audio tour is enjoyable and informative. Lombard Street is a fun sight to see, and the views of San Francisco Bay are breathtaking. Golden Gate park is a real treat to walk around. In the park, be sure to visit the Conservatory of Flowers or the Japanese Tea Garden. There is a new museum opening within the park (DeYoung) so that will be worth a visit. I believe it opens in October.We have a couple of awesome breakfast spots to recommend: Dotties True Blue Cafe on Jones Street. There will most likely be a wait but that's not what you'll remember afterward. Excellent food and service and just a neat place to eat a very hearty breakfast. The other place is The Pork Store--it's at Haight  Ashbury. Again, expect a wait but then expect a fab breakfast in a fun atmosphere. The host (of sorts) was a gem. He checked in with everyone and had a running joke going with each table it seemed. We dined in style at Aliotos one evening and so enjoyed the fresh seafood. Prices were fair for the experience.Fun place to visit in the evening is The Cannery (next to The Argonaut). There's live music around 6pm--we enjoyed two really good bands. It's a courtyard area with a couple of bars so it's an ideal place to sit with your cold drink, listen to the bands and people watch. Lots more to see and do and recommend--that's why we'll be going back soon. Forgot to mention the good breakfast spot across from the hotel. Its called Pergaminos. Very nice indeed.

<Author>coy_coy
<Content>Not bad, great location A quick warning before I start the review.....if your room is in the annex building, use a bellman ! Getting to the other building includes walking out on to the street in front of the hotel and a good 300 yard walk down a busy road. I lost count of the number of people I saw lugging heavy cases, clearly underestimating how far apart the entrances to the 2 separate buildings are.We spent 2 nights in the annex building in August 2005. The room was satisfactory (2 queen size beds) although the decoration was a bit dated. It was kept clean though and we were impressed by the friendly maid service who went out of her way on a few occasions. There is a 24 hour Dennys in the lobby of the annex, where service was dreadfully slow in the mornings when it gets busy. We had a 30 minute wait for food which was not good when you only have a day and a half in the City and want to get out and see some sights. The famous Lombard Street crooked street is walkable too, although the hill you walk up to get there is VERY steep.I can't fault the location of the hotel which was in easy walking distance of Fishermans Wharf, Alcatraz Ferry, Cable car turnaround (where you could catch a cable car all the way into downtown area), The Cannery etc etc. A cab from downtown back to the hotel cost about $9 - worth getting as he tool us speedily over Russian Hill, reminding us of the classic Steve McQueen car chase!We didn't use the pool or main restaurant, but generally we were happy with the hotel. Not exceptional, but functional and close to the action. One last word of warning though - if you bring your car, you will get charged $32 per day which seems to be a common charge in this city. Parking is a nightmare in SF and driving is not too pleasurable either, so its a good idea to leave your car out of the city if you can. We booked our stay through a travel agent and got our parking charge waived, but the guy in front of me checking in went pale when they told him the car park charge!  
<Date>Sep 1, 2005

Lot's of families with kids stay here, so there can be a bit of playful noise about. If you are on a honeymoon or want a quiet romantic weekend, you should probably not stay here.

<Author>helenathome
<Content>to stay or not to stay we stayed at the holiday inn without actually staying there if you know what I mean- our room was in the annnexe around the corner. It was fine and probably a bit less noisy than the main part, but the downside was that we didn't get to use any of the hotel facilities, including the pool, and only discovered the delightful pergamino's cafe over the road for breakfast on day 4.The room was spacious and clean, with a safe and hanging rail for clothes rather than a wardrobe, spacious bathroom (well big enough for us). The annexe had a Denny's restaurant where we ate breakfast the first few days, our son loved it but the food was only average and it was a bit pricey. Still everything about our California holiday was expensive this time round.We had hired a car because we wnated to visit several places independently, rather than take a young boy on too many coach excursions, but after getting lost from the airport (due to some crappy directions given us by our holiday firm) we ended up driving through all the worst and busiest bits of SF, including right down the cnetre of Chinatown! Ultimately, we decided that the car had been a mistake, especially as there is such a good transport network in the city. Fisherman's Wharf was fun, and not as ghastly as a lot of people made out, plus, we had so many other sights to see, including the fab Golden gate Bridge and a trip on the outside of the famous cable car at Powell and Hyde (for which there was a considerable wait, so get there early). Fisherman's Wharf has some nice seafood restaurants, again pricey, and is all on the level, so walkign around is easy. I would certainyl recommend it for families, as there is Pier 39 with the sealions and the ferries for Alcatraz(a must) plus amusement arcade and lots of shops. Also go see Coit Tower - walk up Telegraph Hill if you have the energy(exhausting!) or drive up an then get the lift to the top for some great views. Chinatown a must also, we ate at the wonderful Emperess of China, which has views of Coit Tower and food authentic, decor beautiful and waiters very attentive (good value as well). Visit The Fort underneath the bridge, it's a big former miltary garrison that has been renovated and opened to the public, very inetersting for children and adults alike. Take a city tour early in your trip, it will give you a good account of what the city has to offer and then you can pick and choose where to return. Ate at the Cliff House on the promontary about 5-6 miles from SF, lovley food and superb Pacific coast/beach views. Wrap up warm - SF is very chilly in the morninngs and the fog invariably covers the bridge, although it usually clears by the afternoon - average temp when we were there was 65C (40 degress less than at our friend's house two hours inland!). Woudl return to SF tomorrow if we could, and to the Holiday Inn as well. San Franciscans are an amiable lot, non-conformist and very relaxed about life in general, and SF is the one city in America where you will find interesting house architecture  
<Date>Aug 21, 2005

<Author>Dmun
<Content>Great Location - right in the heart of things This hotel does have an excellent location for exploring the Wharf, catching a cable car etc and has a number of very good restaraunts close by. It can only be a couple of hundred metres to the waterfront. The staff were very friendly and helpful. The rooms were average HI but nothing that I could complain about - generally the usual Holiday Inn standard that you can trust. The pool is quite small but many people probably wont spend much time in the pool in San Fran anyway. Although its relatvely expensive for a Holiday Inn it a very reasonably priced hotel in terms of San Frnasisco. It's right next to the Holiday Inn Express and the Hilton. There is a business centre with free internet access which is nice. There is a restaraunt but we never ate there.Be very careful if buying any camera/ video equipment near the Wharf - it pays to be a well informed buyer. They can smell an opportunity to make a fast 100 + bucks!If going back to SF then I probably would go back to this Hotel. I have stayed at the Civic Centre area in SF on a previous visit but I would say don't do it. There is no comparison in terms of location. The Wharf wins hands down every time. The Civic Centre area is a soup kitchen, blanket dispensing haven for SF's homeless - which is good for them but not what most people will want to experience daily on a trip to California. You could no doubt pay more and get a more upmarket hotel but I doubt the location would be any better any where around the wharf. A good deal all round. Well done Holiday Inn.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't understand bad reviews! Stayed here for 4 nights in June on the way back from Hawaii. We were in the part of the hotel down the road where Denny's resturant was and had no complaints at all about our room. 2 double beds and a reasonable sized bathroom, both of which were kept spottlessly clesn and we didn't have problems with any noise. We didn't use the pool, we didn't have time!Had no problems with any of the staff, found them all to be courteous and helpful when we checked in and out. Ate at the main hotel resturant one night and had a wonderfully cooked meal which was worth every penny. Wine was a tad pricey though.Location was brilliant, one block from fishermans wharf and pier 39. It was also close to the tram, bus and cable car so we could get anywhere really easily. We were shocked at the quality of the public transport. We bought a 3 day travel pass for $15 which meant we could use the trains, trams, buses and cablecars which was worth every penny.We were lucky and had 4 really clear, warm days so had a great time visiting the golden gate bridge and alcatraz (among other things). We both fell in love with the city and would definately stay at the Holiday Inn Fishermans Wharf again.  
<Date>Jul 2, 2005

<Author>spreadhead
<Content>Spent the weekend here for the second time My wife and I stayed here over the weekend for the 2nd time. For the price, the room is acceptable (SF is a pricey city). We usually find that we do a ton of walking there, and sleep well regardless were we stay. We got a double room this time and took our 16 yr old son. The location is ideal for a fun family trip, or a weekend away from rainy Seattle with the wife. Fisherman's warf and Pier 39 are great spots for the kids. We spent a whole day there doing the tourist thing. Sure, the rooms could be nicer or larger. But we were only there to sleep. If you stay in Fisherman,s warf, try the breakfast at peragamo's across the street. They claim to have the best waffles, and they might be. They have the greatest host, Rueban. If your lucky he will grace you with a song and will always make you feel welcome. Breakfast there is a part of our stay everytime. another tip. If you are planning to rent a car, it'll cost you 35/day to park. They have a fantastic metro system here. The historic streetcar stop is a 1/2 block away, next to a walgreen's{unload your digital camera here,and save your pics on CD for a couple bucks!}. The streetcar will take you to market streek, you can get anywere from there in a few minutes. Famous trolly stop 2 blocks. Save that money on parking, take the transit. spend that cash on a boat tour of the bay 2 blocks away you can take a boat around alkatraz and under the golden gate for 10 each. look for a wooden boat captined by Maury. We had a blast and he was cool

<Author>chicago29
<Content>A nice surprise ! We were expecting the worst with this hotel after reading the reviews on trip advisor prior to travelling, but had a nice surprise. We were also roomed in the 'annexe' building on the next street, only a couple of minutes walk from main hotel. We checked in and were offered help across the road with our luggage. Were on the 4th floor in a twin room which had two double/queen sized beds. The en suite was large with bath and shower. There were coffee making facilities, air con, tv, optional 'pay per view' movies and nintendo if you wanted them, and a free newspaper every day. There was also free internet access for as long as you wanted (as long as no one was waiting) in the Holiday Express hotel a few doors down, you just had to show your Holiday Inn key card. We were a five minute walk from a sandy bay, with free museum and great views of the golden gate bridge. Trams went further into the city regularly and there were a multitude of great eating places 5/10 minutes walk away. All the staff and house keeping were polite and helpful. Although on the ground floor there is a 24 hour 'Dennys' restaurant there was never any excess noise, even from the street outside! We would definately stay there again. Also would recommend Pier 39 for unusual shopping, boat trips and eateries and the Bay Shuttle door to door airport service, which you can reserve online with no fee before you travel !!!

The standard of the room was OK but there was a faint smell of smoke and we had quite a busy road outside our room. However, we did not spend a lot of time in the room as we were busy out and about during our stay - a good point is that the hotel is well located for the attractions on Fishermans Wharf and for accessing the transport links into the city. Also, there was a really good guy in the reception of the second building who gave us some excellent information about how to get around the city and some other tourist bits of information. I guess on reflection you do get what you pay for and we didnt pay 5* prices, I would class it as an average place to stay with no frills.

<Author>BJM
<Content>Great Location - that's about it! If you want to stay at the Wharf then the location is excellent, as you are just opposite the Cannery and it is a pleasant stroll to Pier 39 and Ghiradelli Square. The streetcars and cable lines are also short strolls away. However, we had a room overlooking the back of the Cannery and it was very noisey at night. Things from the bars would quieten down by about 2am then the street cleaning vechicles etc would start c. 4.30am! The room itself was as you would expect - clean, good size with all the usual amenities. Staff were pleasant and helpful. Next time I think I would stay abit further from Wharf (transport in San Fransico excellent so no trouble getting around) to get a quieter nights sleep. Try the Buena Vista restaurant/bar overlooking the cable car line (near Gharadelli Square) - excellent breakfasts and views.

<Author>JimC
<Content>Be very circumspect if staying here We arrived at this hotel on 2nd November. Could not fault the room itself,however, at approx. 3.30am every morning the dustbins in the hotel opposite are emptied and the noise is awful. Furthermore, with the strike still taking place, we were woken at 7am every morning by a picket using a bull horn informing us that this was our early morning call and again at 10pm wishing us  a good night, amusing if your reading this, but not if you are listening to it! Furthermore, this hotel seems to have a penchant for school children staying. On the 5th Nov. about 100 Chinese school children arrived, and both the children and their tutors could speak very little, if any, English and had nothing but contempt for other guests. This became apparant on the first evening when they ran up and down the hotel corridors slamming doors and making one hell of a noise up to 11pm. The noise started up again at 5.40am when the arose for breakfast. But, the real crunch came on Sat night when the noise started at about 9pm and went on until 3.10 am, and then started up again at 5.40am.I phoned the front desk twice, my wife ( and other guests) confronted the children in the corridors, but to no avail, (they didn't understand English) and finally I went down to the front desk (in my pyjamas) to complain at about 1.30am. I completed a complaint form, and whilst I was doing this youngsters were running around the foyer, jumping up and down on the furniture and shouting and yelling at each other. I asked the clerk why she didn't do something about it and said she was unable to do so as it was the job of Security. The security guard asked me if I would like to change my room, but what good would that have done as the noise effect was throughout the hotel, and we were leaving at 9am anyway. The next morning when speaking to other guests it would seem that everyone had complained. At check out I again complained most strenousely, and after a bit of a kerfuffle I was given compensation. I also confronted one of the tutors and gave him a mouthful, but probably didn't do much good as his English was limited, but it made me feel a bit better.There were at least two lots of schools that checked in that week.I suppose it goes without saying, that I would not recommend this hotel.

<Author>sharima
<Content>Good and bad, depends what's important to you We stayed at the Holiday Inn over Labor Day weekend, and had a great time in San Francisco. The hotel had some really good points, and some not so good points. First of all, it was 1 short block from where the action is at Ghiradelli Square, the Wharf, Pier 39, etc. The bad part is that when you check in at the main desk, you may find out that your room is in a wing that's located across the street from the main section. That means parking and dragging your luggage down the sidewalk and across the street to the other wing (a little embarrassing and inconvienient). Our room was nice, though we had no view at all. Noise was not a problem at all--very quiet where we were (except that the entry doors tend to slam shut). We were there to shower and sleep, which was fine--and as long as you don't expect much more than that, it's a good location.

It is close to the Trolley Bus pick-up point - get a 3-day pass for $15. It is fantastic value as you can use the trolley bus, cable car and local 'muni' buses.I would not hesitate in staying here again.

<Author>Standby4321
<Content>Decent value; excellent location We've stayed several times at the Holiday Inn, Fisherman's Wharf and found it to be an excellent value on the Internet Saver rate off the Six Continents Hotels website. Our stay during the last weekend of January 2004 was in the main building at a rate of $85/night. The room was clean, furnishings in good repair and our room overlooked the Cannery. The breakfast buffet is decent and Priority Club members receive vouchers for 50% off the regular $15.95 price, (so be sure to join Priority Club before you make your reservation at the hotel.)Note that there is an annex to this hotel in a separate building. We have never stayed in it and it would not be our preference to do so. There is also an executive floor on the fifth level of the main building with key card access if you want something a little more than the standard offering.The HI Fisherman's Wharf is within easy walking distance to Fisherman's Wharf and the cable cars. We like to walk a lot and so we also found it easy enough to take in much of the North Beach neighborhood and Chinatown. If you can get a good rate, it's a solid value. If you are looking at rack rates, then there are more premium properties in the area that you should research.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel-good value. Stayed here Nov. 14-21, 2003 on the business floor during a conference. Clean, well-apponted room. Staff busy with high-volume custom, but still very helpful. Well located, near cable-car terminal, Pier 39; easy access to Financial District with complimentary shuttle. Plenty of MUNI stops nearby. Good breakfast buffet. Dining room deserted at night; plenty of good eateries nearby. Some traffic noise at night--but, hey, this is a downtown location adjacent to two busy streets. If you want quiet, try Carmel. If you're driving, leave your car in the lot and take transit; traffic in SF is unbelievable. Lots of alternatives nearby--BW, Marriott, Sheraton, Hilton, Hotel Argonaut, etc.

<Author>Maggie/WI
<Content>A Good Place for Us We stayed at this hotel right after 9/11/01 and remember it being fine for our needs. Returned there Oct. of this year for two nights and again it was just fine for what we were looking for. Contrary to what previous posters have said, we found the staff to be very cordial and accommodating. The room was average but it was clean and had everything we needed -- we were there as tourists to the wharf and didn't spend alot of time in the room so anything fancier/more expensive would have been wasted on us. If we were to return, we'd stay there again.
